Suggested Intervention
Following are the suggested interventions for the 4 key areas identified for Andhra Pradesh in Grade 3

Click on the group to expand and see the summary.

1. Enhance student learning outcomes through innovative teaching strategies
Language

  • C-10.5 Reads short stories and comprehends their meaning - by identifying characters, storyline and what the author wants to say - on their ownN/A

    Intervention : Multi-Sensory Learning Approaches: Incorporate auditory, visual, and kinesthetic activities such as interactive storytelling, picture-word association, and tactile learning materials. Play-Based Literacy and Numeracy Activities: Engage students in phonics-based games, counting with manipulatives, and story sequencing tasks to strengthen foundational competencies. Scaffolded Learning Support: Implement structured progression in activities, gradually increasing complexity to aid comprehension and skill development. Targeted Small Group Instruction: Provide focused interventions for struggling learners through guided reading, math centers, and one-on-one teacher interactions. Parental Engagement: Develop take-home literacy and numeracy kits to reinforce skills beyond the classroom. Assessment and Monitoring (Aligned with Holistic Progress Card - HPC) Assessment Tools: Play-based observation, storytelling retelling, number sense activities, checklists, and teacher portfolios. HPC Alignment: Evaluating early literacy, numeracy, social-emotional learning, and motor skills through continuous observation.Read More

2. Use diverse assessments, such as peer and self-assessments, to support holistic development.

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use self assessment as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : 1 - Capacity Building for Teachers on Self-Assessment Techniques Training Workshops on HPC Implementation: Conduct mandatory teacher training on using Holistic Progress Cards at different stages (Foundational, Preparatory, Middle, Secondary). Utilize NISHTHA and DIKSHA platforms for capacity-building modules on student self-assessment. Integration into Classroom Pedagogy: Develop teacher guides with subject-specific self-assessment rubrics aligned with HPC. Introduce peer learning groups for teachers to exchange best practices on self-assessment. Incentivizing Self-Assessment Adoption: Recognize and reward teachers who effectively implement student self-assessment. Encourage micro-innovations in self-assessment through action research projects. 2 - Implementing Stage-Specific Self-Assessment Tools for Students: Preparatory Stage (Grades 3–5): Introduce classroom participation charts where students rate themselves based on engagement in activities. Self-tutoring videos Use visual self-assessment boards (smiley faces, stars, colors) to encourage reflection. Conduct weekly self-reflection sessions where students share their progress. Middle Stage (Grades 6–8): Implement student-led peer feedback mechanisms where students assess each others participation and behavior. Self-tutoring videos: Develop subject-specific self-assessment checklists, focusing on conceptual understanding and skills. Introduce student reflection journals aligned with HPC performance descriptors (Stream, Mountain, Sky). Secondary Stage (Grades 9–12): Encourage students to create their own learning goals and track progress using self-evaluation rubrics. Foster student-led discussions on performance improvement in group settings. Establish mentorship programs where senior students guide juniors on self-assessment. 3 - Classroom Strategies for Embedding Self-Assessment: Daily Reflection Practices: Use classroom activities and games where students reflect on what they learned and rate their understanding. Use Two Stars and a Wish like programs for self-assessment where students highlight two strengths and one area for improvement for self and peers. Collaborative Goal-Setting and Reflection: Conduct monthly student-teacher conferences where students present their self-assessments. Encourage peer accountability-students remind and support each other in following classroom expectations. Use of Digital Tools for Self-Assessment: Integrate Google Forms, Padlet, or Learning Management Systems (LMS) for student self-evaluation. Utilize DIKSHAs digital HPC format for structured student reflection. 4 - Monitoring and Support System for Teachers: Classroom Observations and Feedback: Implement peer and mentor teacher observations to track the integration of self-assessment. Provide real-time feedback and coaching for teachers struggling to implement self-assessment. Inclusion of Self-Assessment in Teacher Appraisals: Make self-assessment integration a key parameter in teacher performance reviews. Recognize and document best self-assessment practices through academic portfolios. School Leadership Support: Principals and senior educators should actively model self-assessment practices for teachers. Organize Self-Assessment Best Practices sharing forums within the school cluster or district.Read More

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use peer assessment as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : Early Childhood Stage (Foundational Years- Ages 3-8): Play-Based Peer Assessment: Encourage students to describe their friends work in simple terms. Use buddy reflections where children express what they liked about their peers activities. Interactive Group Activities: Implement collaborative storytelling, group art projects, and shared play-based tasks where children provide basic feedback. Teacher-Guided Peer Interaction: Teachers can facilitate verbal feedback using visual tools smiley cards, thumbs up-down, or storytelling boards to make peer assessment age appropriate. Parental Involvement: Use the Holistic Progress Card to inform parents about their childs social interactions and peer engagement. Middle Childhood Stage (Preparatory and Middle Stage- Ages 8-14): Structured Peer Feedback in Classroom Activities: Introduce peer feedback rubrics for activities like group projects, role-plays, and inquiry-based learning tasks. Peer Assessment in Holistic Progress Card Evaluations: Train students to self-assess and assess peers in project-based learning, quizzes, and group tasks as part of formative assessments. Conduct monthly peer assessment reflections integrated into the HPC records. Training Teachers to Facilitate Peer Assessments: Organize teacher training sessions under NISHTHA and DIKSHA portals on integrating peer assessment techniques. Create state-led mentoring programs for peer assessment best practices. Technology-Enabled Peer Feedback: Use AI-based interactive tools for students to give feedback on each others projects. Encourage Google Forms, Padlet, and Kahoot-based peer assessments for quizzes and reflections. Adolescence Stage (Secondary Stage- Ages 14-18): Student-Led Peer Assessment Framework: Introduce student peer mentors who evaluate class participation, presentations, and group discussions. Implement peer grading in essays, research work, and portfolio assessments with teacher oversight. Advanced Peer Assessment in Project-Based Learning: Use peer review in science experiments, history projects, and creative writing assignments. Develop cross-school peer collaboration (exchanging feedback between students from different schools through virtual platforms). Developing a Culture of Constructive Criticism: Train students in giving and receiving constructive feedback without bias. Use peer-led reflections after classroom debates, discussions, and competitions. AI-Based Holistic Progress Card for Tracking Peer Assessments: Develop an interactive AI tool where students rate their own and peers progress based on specific skills. Include peer feedback as part of career guidance recommendations. Teacher Capacity Building: 1 - Mandatory Training on Peer Assessment Include peer assessment as a core component in all teacher training programs under NISHTHA, DIKSHA, and state-level education training. 2 - Policy Mandate for Peer Assessment in Progress Cards Ensure that peer assessment is included in holistic report cards under the guidelines of PARAKH, NCERT. Schools must submit annual reports on peer assessment practices to the education department. 3 - Reducing Resistance to Peer Assessment Conduct awareness sessions for teachers and parents on the benefits of peer assessment. Organize exchange programs where schools implementing successful peer assessment strategies mentor others. Monthly review of peer assessment practices in schools via teacher self-reports and student feedback. Integration of peer assessment evidence in the Holistic Progress Card. Randomized classroom observations by education department officials to assess peer assessment implementation.Read More

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use Project Work as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : 1 - Capacity Building and Teacher Training Mandatory Professional Development on Project-Based Learning (PBL): Organize training programs for teachers at district and state levels on designing and implementing project-based assessments. Use DIKSHA and SWAYAM online platforms to offer self-paced modules on project-based learning. Partner with State Councils of Educational Research and Training (SCERTs) and universities to incorporate project-based learning training in teacher education programs. Peer Learning and Best Practices Sharing: Establish Teacher Learning Circles in schools for experience-sharing and collaborative project planning. Create a repository of successful project-based assessment models that teachers can adapt to their subjects. 2 - Integration of Project Work in Assessment Policies Inclusion of Project Work in Formative and Summative Assessments: Ensure that a significant portion of student assessment includes project work, allowing students to demonstrate their learning in creative ways. Teachers should provide graded, structured project assignments that align with different learning levels. Introduce varied assessment methods such as oral presentations, digital projects, and hands-on demonstrations to cater to diverse learning needs. Mandatory Implementation of Skill and Real-Life Projects: Ensure students complete a minimum of three interdisciplinary projects per academic year, linked to real-world applications. Design projects that focus on local issues, environmental studies, history, and community engagement (eg, conducting surveys, mapping local resources, investigating historical events). 3 - Leveraging Technology for Project-Based Learning Use of Virtual Labs and Digital Tools: Encourage the use of virtual labs, digital simulations, and open educational resources to facilitate project-based learning. Provide access to collaborative tools like Google Classroom, Padlet, and local e-learning platforms to support project submissions and feedback. AI and Peer Learning Platforms for Project Guidance: Introduce AI-powered chatbots and peer discussion forums for students to seek guidance on project work. Promote the use of online research tools and digital archives for data collection and analysis. 4 - School-Level Initiatives for Project Implementation Annual Project Showcase Events: Organize a skills fair or exhibition where students present their projects to parents, community members, and stakeholders. Encourage interdisciplinary projects that integrate science, technology, arts, and humanities. Incentivizing Project-Based Learning for Teachers and Students: Recognize teachers who effectively implement project-based assessments through certificates, awards, or career growth opportunities. Establish a Student Innovation Fund to support project-based learning initiatives in schools. 5 - Policy-Level Changes for Sustainable Implementation Strengthening Educational Policies at State and National Levels: Integrate project-based learning guidelines into state curriculum frameworks to ensure consistent implementation. Encourage state education boards and SCERTs to develop model project-based assessment templates. Monitoring and Evaluation for Continuous Improvement: Implement regular reviews and feedback mechanisms to track the effectiveness of project-based learning. Conduct teacher and student surveys to assess the impact of project work on learning outcomes. Self-tutoring videos and guides for TPDRead More

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use Portfolio as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : 1 - Capacity Building for Teachers Training Under PARAKH and NCERT Guidelines: Develop teacher training modules focused on portfolio-based assessment. Offer online capacity-building programs through DIKSHA and SWAYAM. Providing Structured Portfolio Templates: Design subject-wise templates aligned with NCERTs Holistic Progress Card (HPC), covering academic and socio-emotional learning. Promote digital portfolio tools (Google Drive, Padlet, OneNote, etc.) for easy documentation. Collaborative Learning for Teachers: Organize peer-led workshops to share best practices in portfolio usage. Implement classroom demonstration sessions on portfolio-based assessment. 2 - Integration with Curriculum and Assessment Embedding Portfolios in Formative Assessments: Link with PARAKH-aligned learning outcomes to ensure portfolios reflect conceptual understanding, critical thinking, and creativity. Use portfolios in multidisciplinary learning, STEM projects, and experiential learning activities. Portfolio as a Student Reflection Tool: Encourage students to track their learning journey by documenting progress in subject areas and co-curricular activities. Implement self-assessment and peer-review practices to promote deeper engagement. Portfolio Presentation and Showcasing: Introduce Portfolio Days where students present their work to peers, teachers, and parents. Integrate portfolios into student-led conferences, aligning with HPCs focus on student voice and agency. 3 - Student Ownership and Participation Developing Classroom Culture for Portfolio Maintenance: Establish Portfolio Corners in classrooms for organizing student work. Encourage students to maintain personal progress files, fostering accountability. Promoting Peer Learning and Reflection: Implement peer review sessions where students provide constructive feedback. Encourage students to include teacher comments, peer feedback, and self-reflections in their portfolios. Leveraging Digital Portfolios for Documentation: Introduce e-portfolios through mobile apps or school-based learning platforms. Use QR codes for easy digital access to student work samples. 4 - Strengthening Parent-Teacher Collaboration Using Portfolios in Parent-Teacher Meetings (PTMs): Replace traditional report card discussions with portfolio-based progress tracking. Organize portfolio exhibitions, showcasing student learning beyond academics. Parental Involvement in Student Learning: Provide guidance to parents on reviewing and contributing to student portfolios. Encourage students to document home-learning experiences, projects, and extracurricular activities. Recognizing and Celebrating Student Growth: Introduce monthly recognition for outstanding portfolios. Organize student-led portfolio presentations, reinforcing ownership and confidence. 5 - Policy-Level Support and Sustainable Implementation NCERT and State Education Boards to Issue Portfolio Guidelines: Establish standardized evaluation rubrics for portfolio assessment under PARAKH. Encourage alignment with HPCs multidimensional assessment approach. School-Level Monitoring and Support: Form Portfolio Committees to track implementation. Conduct quarterly portfolio reviews to ensure consistent usage. Aligning Portfolios with NEP 2020s Holistic Progress Card (HPC): Ensure portfolios reflect cognitive, socio-emotional, and creative learning as outlined in HPC. Use portfolios as evidence of students evolving competencies beyond examinations.Read More

3. Integrate sports and the arts into the curriculum to foster joyful and creative learning.

  • Percentage of Teachers who never or rarely use Sports integrated learning padagogyN/A

    Intervention : Workshops and Training Programs: Conduct capacity-building workshops for teachers to integrate sports with core subjects. Organize professional development programs focusing on experiential learning, sports pedagogy, and creative teaching methods. Encourage peer learning through best practice sharing sessions. Resource Development: Provide structured lesson plans that integrate sports and physical activities with academic concepts. Develop digital and print resources demonstrating sports-based teaching strategies. Multidisciplinary Approach: Promote interdisciplinary teaching by using sports and arts to explain mathematical, scientific, and linguistic concepts. Align lesson plans with experiential learning principles. Preparatory Stage Implementation: Integrate structured physical activities, Yoga, and creative movement-based learning in the school schedule. Introduce warm-up activities linked to cognitive learning outcomes. Flexible Classroom Environment: Encourage active learning spaces where students explore concepts through movement and play. Foster an inclusive and engaging learning atmosphere using kinesthetic learning techniques. Collaboration and Mentorship: Facilitate collaborations between subject teachers, sports educators, and creative professionals to co-design lessons. Establish mentorship programs where trained teachers guide their peers in implementing sports-integrated teaching methods. Feedback and Assessment Mechanism: Utilize formative assessments to gauge student engagement and learning outcomes. Implement the Holistic Progress Card (HPC) developed by PARAKH (NCERT) to track students progress in cognitive, emotional, and physical domains. Encourage self and peer assessment methods in sports-integrated learning. Recognition and Incentives: Introduce awards and certifications for teachers demonstrating innovative teaching practices. Establish a platform to showcase success stories of teachers effectively integrating sports in pedagogy. Government Schemes and Policies Supporting Implementation: National Education Policy (NEP) 2020: Emphasizes experiential and sports-integrated learning for holistic development. Samagra Shiksha Abhiyan (SSA): Supports innovative teaching methodologies, including activity-based learning. Khelo India Program: Encourages schools to integrate sports in education for holistic student growth. Fit India Movement: Promotes physical fitness and activity-based learning in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of Teachers who never or rarely use Arts integrated learning padagogyN/A

    Intervention : Workshops and Capacity Building: Conduct interactive workshops highlighting the benefits of arts integration. Train teachers on strategies to incorporate visual arts, music, drama, and movement into core subjects. Resource Development and Dissemination: Provide structured lesson plans that integrate arts into various subjects. Develop digital repositories with exemplar lesson plans and video demonstrations. Expert-Led Sessions: Engage professional artists and experienced educators to share best practices. Conduct classroom demonstrations showcasing effective arts integration. Multidisciplinary Learning Approaches: Encourage interdisciplinary projects that link arts with STEM, humanities, and social sciences. Implement storytelling in language learning, dance in math, and drama in history lessons. Aesthetic and Cultural Development (Anandamaya Kosha): Organize cultural immersion programs to deepen students artistic sensibilities. Facilitate exposure to classical and folk art forms, emphasizing Indias rich cultural heritage. Structured Practices in Traditional Arts: Introduce structured inquiry-based learning through traditional performing and visual arts. Align practices with values of discipline, collaboration, and aesthetic appreciation. Flexible and Collaborative Learning Spaces: Promote self-expression and creative collaboration through project-based learning. Create dedicated spaces for art-based exploration in schools. Feedback Mechanism and Observational Assessments: Implement student engagement and creativity rubrics for classroom assessment. Conduct peer observations and provide constructive feedback for teachers. Performance Review through Art-Based Assessments: Use diverse assessment tools such as portfolios, performance-based tasks, and exhibitions. Align with the Holistic Progress Card (HPC) framework developed by PARAKH (NCERT) to evaluate cognitive, affective, and psychomotor development. Establish awards for innovative arts-integrated teaching practices. Highlight exemplary teachers in newsletters, school events, and government reports. Inquiry-Driven Science Activities: Encourage student-led experiments, field explorations, and collaborative investigations. Integrated Arts and Movement: Utilize role-playing, storytelling through puppetry, and kinesthetic learning to reinforce comprehension and cognitive engagement. Technology-Enabled Learning: Introduce age-appropriate digital tools, educational apps, and virtual labs to enhance concept retention. HPC Alignment: Tracking literacy development, logical reasoning, problem-solving ability, and scientific curiosity using rubrics and performance-based assessments.Read More

2. Use diverse assessments, such as peer and self-assessments, to support holistic development.

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use self assessment as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : 1 - Capacity Building for Teachers on Self-Assessment Techniques Training Workshops on HPC Implementation: Conduct mandatory teacher training on using Holistic Progress Cards at different stages (Foundational, Preparatory, Middle, Secondary). Utilize NISHTHA and DIKSHA platforms for capacity-building modules on student self-assessment. Integration into Classroom Pedagogy: Develop teacher guides with subject-specific self-assessment rubrics aligned with HPC. Introduce peer learning groups for teachers to exchange best practices on self-assessment. Incentivizing Self-Assessment Adoption: Recognize and reward teachers who effectively implement student self-assessment. Encourage micro-innovations in self-assessment through action research projects. 2 - Implementing Stage-Specific Self-Assessment Tools for Students: Preparatory Stage (Grades 3–5): Introduce classroom participation charts where students rate themselves based on engagement in activities. Self-tutoring videos Use visual self-assessment boards (smiley faces, stars, colors) to encourage reflection. Conduct weekly self-reflection sessions where students share their progress. Middle Stage (Grades 6–8): Implement student-led peer feedback mechanisms where students assess each others participation and behavior. Self-tutoring videos: Develop subject-specific self-assessment checklists, focusing on conceptual understanding and skills. Introduce student reflection journals aligned with HPC performance descriptors (Stream, Mountain, Sky). Secondary Stage (Grades 9–12): Encourage students to create their own learning goals and track progress using self-evaluation rubrics. Foster student-led discussions on performance improvement in group settings. Establish mentorship programs where senior students guide juniors on self-assessment. 3 - Classroom Strategies for Embedding Self-Assessment: Daily Reflection Practices: Use classroom activities and games where students reflect on what they learned and rate their understanding. Use Two Stars and a Wish like programs for self-assessment where students highlight two strengths and one area for improvement for self and peers. Collaborative Goal-Setting and Reflection: Conduct monthly student-teacher conferences where students present their self-assessments. Encourage peer accountability-students remind and support each other in following classroom expectations. Use of Digital Tools for Self-Assessment: Integrate Google Forms, Padlet, or Learning Management Systems (LMS) for student self-evaluation. Utilize DIKSHAs digital HPC format for structured student reflection. 4 - Monitoring and Support System for Teachers: Classroom Observations and Feedback: Implement peer and mentor teacher observations to track the integration of self-assessment. Provide real-time feedback and coaching for teachers struggling to implement self-assessment. Inclusion of Self-Assessment in Teacher Appraisals: Make self-assessment integration a key parameter in teacher performance reviews. Recognize and document best self-assessment practices through academic portfolios. School Leadership Support: Principals and senior educators should actively model self-assessment practices for teachers. Organize Self-Assessment Best Practices sharing forums within the school cluster or district.Read More

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use peer assessment as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : Early Childhood Stage (Foundational Years- Ages 3-8): Play-Based Peer Assessment: Encourage students to describe their friends work in simple terms. Use buddy reflections where children express what they liked about their peers activities. Interactive Group Activities: Implement collaborative storytelling, group art projects, and shared play-based tasks where children provide basic feedback. Teacher-Guided Peer Interaction: Teachers can facilitate verbal feedback using visual tools smiley cards, thumbs up-down, or storytelling boards to make peer assessment age appropriate. Parental Involvement: Use the Holistic Progress Card to inform parents about their childs social interactions and peer engagement. Middle Childhood Stage (Preparatory and Middle Stage- Ages 8-14): Structured Peer Feedback in Classroom Activities: Introduce peer feedback rubrics for activities like group projects, role-plays, and inquiry-based learning tasks. Peer Assessment in Holistic Progress Card Evaluations: Train students to self-assess and assess peers in project-based learning, quizzes, and group tasks as part of formative assessments. Conduct monthly peer assessment reflections integrated into the HPC records. Training Teachers to Facilitate Peer Assessments: Organize teacher training sessions under NISHTHA and DIKSHA portals on integrating peer assessment techniques. Create state-led mentoring programs for peer assessment best practices. Technology-Enabled Peer Feedback: Use AI-based interactive tools for students to give feedback on each others projects. Encourage Google Forms, Padlet, and Kahoot-based peer assessments for quizzes and reflections. Adolescence Stage (Secondary Stage- Ages 14-18): Student-Led Peer Assessment Framework: Introduce student peer mentors who evaluate class participation, presentations, and group discussions. Implement peer grading in essays, research work, and portfolio assessments with teacher oversight. Advanced Peer Assessment in Project-Based Learning: Use peer review in science experiments, history projects, and creative writing assignments. Develop cross-school peer collaboration (exchanging feedback between students from different schools through virtual platforms). Developing a Culture of Constructive Criticism: Train students in giving and receiving constructive feedback without bias. Use peer-led reflections after classroom debates, discussions, and competitions. AI-Based Holistic Progress Card for Tracking Peer Assessments: Develop an interactive AI tool where students rate their own and peers progress based on specific skills. Include peer feedback as part of career guidance recommendations. Teacher Capacity Building: 1 - Mandatory Training on Peer Assessment Include peer assessment as a core component in all teacher training programs under NISHTHA, DIKSHA, and state-level education training. 2 - Policy Mandate for Peer Assessment in Progress Cards Ensure that peer assessment is included in holistic report cards under the guidelines of PARAKH, NCERT. Schools must submit annual reports on peer assessment practices to the education department. 3 - Reducing Resistance to Peer Assessment Conduct awareness sessions for teachers and parents on the benefits of peer assessment. Organize exchange programs where schools implementing successful peer assessment strategies mentor others. Monthly review of peer assessment practices in schools via teacher self-reports and student feedback. Integration of peer assessment evidence in the Holistic Progress Card. Randomized classroom observations by education department officials to assess peer assessment implementation.Read More

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use Project Work as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : 1 - Capacity Building and Teacher Training Mandatory Professional Development on Project-Based Learning (PBL): Organize training programs for teachers at district and state levels on designing and implementing project-based assessments. Use DIKSHA and SWAYAM online platforms to offer self-paced modules on project-based learning. Partner with State Councils of Educational Research and Training (SCERTs) and universities to incorporate project-based learning training in teacher education programs. Peer Learning and Best Practices Sharing: Establish Teacher Learning Circles in schools for experience-sharing and collaborative project planning. Create a repository of successful project-based assessment models that teachers can adapt to their subjects. 2 - Integration of Project Work in Assessment Policies Inclusion of Project Work in Formative and Summative Assessments: Ensure that a significant portion of student assessment includes project work, allowing students to demonstrate their learning in creative ways. Teachers should provide graded, structured project assignments that align with different learning levels. Introduce varied assessment methods such as oral presentations, digital projects, and hands-on demonstrations to cater to diverse learning needs. Mandatory Implementation of Skill and Real-Life Projects: Ensure students complete a minimum of three interdisciplinary projects per academic year, linked to real-world applications. Design projects that focus on local issues, environmental studies, history, and community engagement (eg, conducting surveys, mapping local resources, investigating historical events). 3 - Leveraging Technology for Project-Based Learning Use of Virtual Labs and Digital Tools: Encourage the use of virtual labs, digital simulations, and open educational resources to facilitate project-based learning. Provide access to collaborative tools like Google Classroom, Padlet, and local e-learning platforms to support project submissions and feedback. AI and Peer Learning Platforms for Project Guidance: Introduce AI-powered chatbots and peer discussion forums for students to seek guidance on project work. Promote the use of online research tools and digital archives for data collection and analysis. 4 - School-Level Initiatives for Project Implementation Annual Project Showcase Events: Organize a skills fair or exhibition where students present their projects to parents, community members, and stakeholders. Encourage interdisciplinary projects that integrate science, technology, arts, and humanities. Incentivizing Project-Based Learning for Teachers and Students: Recognize teachers who effectively implement project-based assessments through certificates, awards, or career growth opportunities. Peer Observation and Feedback System: Facilitate structured classroom observations for teachers to learn from one another. Digital Training Resources: Use platforms like DIKSHA for online behavioral management modules. Holistic Progress Card (HPC): Integrate PARAKH NCERTs framework to assess teachers effectiveness in classroom behavior management. Right to Education (RTE) Act: Bans corporal punishment and promotes positive discipline. National Initiative for School Heads and Teachers Holistic Advancement (NISHTHA): Offers structured training on behavioral management. PM eVIDYA: Provides online modules on effective classroom management strategies. Integrated Teacher Education Programme (ITEP): Focuses on pre-service teacher training, including classroom behavior management. Adolescence Education Programme (AEP): Addresses behavioral challenges and positive discipline in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session/workshop on Managing and understanding Adolescent behaviourN/A

    Intervention : Workshops on Adolescent Psychology and Challenges: Train teachers in understanding hormonal, emotional, and cognitive changes in adolescents. Educate teachers on cyber safety, peer pressure, and substance abuse risks. Peer Counseling Programs: Appoint trained student peer counselors to support adolescent students. Organize interactive sessions with psychologists and social workers. Parental Awareness Sessions: Conduct joint teacher-parent workshops on adolescent behavior. Provide resource materials on adolescent development and parenting strategies. Adolescence Education Program (AEP) by NCERT promotes adolescent awareness in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session or workshop for parents around understanding their children better or managing their behaviourN/A

    Intervention : Mandatory Parental Awareness Workshops: Conduct quarterly parenting sessions in collaboration with mental health experts. Provide behavioral guidance through digital resources and parenting handbooks. Building Strong School-Parent Partnerships: Introduce regular parent-teacher meetings to discuss child behavior and well-being. Create WhatsApp groups or digital forums for parents to share experiences and solutions. Counseling Support for Parents: Establish parent counseling helplines for behavioral concerns. Offer one-on-one sessions for parents struggling with behavioral management. NEP 2020 stresses the role of parents in holistic child development.Read More

  • Percentage of school does not offer any regular Professional Development sessions for teaching staffN/A

    Intervention : Structured CPD Framework: Implement annual Continuing Professional Development (CPD) sessions, ensuring teachers complete 50 hours as mandated by NEP 2020. Digital Learning Platforms: Promote DIKSHA, SWAYAM, NISHTHA, and PM eVIDYA for continuous, certification-based upskilling. Blended Learning Approach: Combine online and offline professional development programs, including workshops and interactive training. Reflective Practice and Peer Learning: Establish teacher learning circles, conduct peer observations, and introduce mentoring programs for knowledge sharing. Subject-Specific Training: Align CPD sessions with NCF 2023, focusing on competency-based teaching, assessment strategies, and student engagement. Expert-Led Workshops: Collaborate with NCERT, SCERTs, CBSE, and state education bodies to conduct regular training with education experts. Integration with Holistic Progress Card (HPC): Use PARAKH NCERTs professional development assessment tools to track teacher progress. NISHTHA (National Initiative for School Heads and Teachers Holistic Advancement): Large-scale teacher training aligned with NEP 2020. DIKSHA (Digital Infrastructure for Knowledge Sharing): Provides free teacher training modules. SWAYAM (Study Webs of Active-Learning for Young Aspiring Minds): Online CPD courses with certification. PM eVIDYA: Digital learning initiative including teacher training. National Professional Standards for Teachers (NPST): Establishes quality benchmarks for teacher development. NCERT CPD Modules: Online and offline training resources for subject-specific pedagogy. Rashtriya Madhyamik Shiksha Abhiyan (RMSA): Funds teacher training programs at the secondary level.Read More

Career Exploration and Applied Skills: Offer exposure to various career pathways, entrepreneurship training, and hands-on skill-building workshops. Assessment and Monitoring (Aligned with Holistic Progress Card - HPC) Assessment Tools: Rubric-based writing assessments, performance-based math evaluations, project-based science tasks, multimedia presentations. HPC Alignment: Measuring conceptual understanding, critical thinking, creativity, digital literacy, and applied learning competencies. Teacher Capacity Building and Community Involvement: • Teacher Training: Workshops on differentiated instruction, competency-based learning, active learning strategies, and formative assessments. • Parental Engagement: Home-based learning kits, community reading programs, numeracy games, and digital literacy initiatives. • Community Support: Collaboration with local organizations, libraries, and resource centers to enhance learning opportunities. • Peer Learning Networks: Establishing teacher learning communities for knowledge exchange and best practice sharing.Read More

2. Use diverse assessments, such as peer and self-assessments, to support holistic development.

  • Percentage of Teacher who never or rarely use self assessment as a tool for assessing studentsN/A

    Intervention : 1 - Capacity Building for Teachers on Self-Assessment Techniques Training Workshops on HPC Implementation: Conduct mandatory teacher training on using Holistic Progress Cards at different stages (Foundational, Preparatory, Middle, Secondary). Utilize NISHTHA and DIKSHA platforms for capacity-building modules on student self-assessment. Integration into Classroom Pedagogy: Develop teacher guides with subject-specific self-assessment rubrics aligned with HPC. Introduce peer learning groups for teachers to exchange best practices on self-assessment. Incentivizing Self-Assessment Adoption: Recognize and reward teachers who effectively implement student self-assessment. Encourage micro-innovations in self-assessment through action research projects. 2 - Implementing Stage-Specific Self-Assessment Tools for Students: Preparatory Stage (Grades 3–5): Introduce classroom participation charts where students rate themselves based on engagement in activities. Self-tutoring videos Use visual self-assessment boards (smiley faces, stars, colors) to encourage reflection. Conduct weekly self-reflection sessions where students share their progress. Middle Stage (Grades 6–8): Implement student-led peer feedback mechanisms where students assess each others participation and behavior. Self-tutoring videos: Develop subject-specific self-assessment checklists, focusing on conceptual understanding and skills. Introduce student reflection journals aligned with HPC performance descriptors (Stream, Mountain, Sky). Secondary Stage (Grades 9–12): Encourage students to create their own learning goals and track progress using self-evaluation rubrics. Foster student-led discussions on performance improvement in group settings. Establish mentorship programs where senior students guide juniors on self-assessment. 3 - Classroom Strategies for Embedding Self-Assessment: Daily Reflection Practices: Use classroom activities and games where students reflect on what they learned and rate their understanding. Use Two Stars and a Wish like programs for self-assessment where students highlight two strengths and one area for improvement for self and peers. Collaborative Goal-Setting and Reflection: Conduct monthly student-teacher conferences where students present their self-assessments. Encourage peer accountability-students remind and support each other in following classroom expectations. Use of Digital Tools for Self-Assessment: Integrate Google Forms, Padlet, or Learning Management Systems (LMS) for student self-evaluation. Utilize DIKSHAs digital HPC format for structured student reflection. 4 - Monitoring and Support System for Teachers: Classroom Observations and Feedback: Implement peer and mentor teacher observations to track the integration of self-assessment. Provide real-time feedback and coaching for teachers struggling to implement self-assessment. Inclusion of Self-Assessment in Teacher Appraisals: Make self-assessment integration a key parameter in teacher performance reviews. Recognize and document best self-assessment practices through academic portfolios. School Leadership Support: Principals and senior educators should actively model self-assessment practices for teachers. Organize Self-Assessment Best Practices sharing forums within the school cluster or district.Read More

    Intervention : Early Childhood Stage (Foundational Years- Ages 3-8): Play-Based Peer Assessment: Encourage students to describe their friends work in simple terms. Adolescence Stage (Secondary Stage- Ages 14-18): Student-Led Peer Assessment Framework: Introduce student peer mentors who evaluate class participation, presentations, and group discussions. Implement peer grading in essays, research work, and portfolio assessments with teacher oversight. DIKSHA Portal: A digital platform offering structured teacher training courses. National Teacher Platform (NTP): Supports CPD with certified online courses. Rashtriya Madhyamik Shiksha Abhiyan (RMSA): Focuses on in-service teacher training for secondary education. PM eVidya: Enhances digital learning access for teachers and students. National Institute of Open Schooling (NIOS) D.El.Ed Program: Supports professional development for untrained teachers. Pandit Madan Mohan Malaviya National Mission on Teachers and Teaching (PMMMNMTT): Aims at improving the quality of teacher education.Read More

  • Percentage of teachers do not participate in the Mentoring and Peer Observation and Coaching as part of a formal school management in BRCs or CRCs activity in las 12 months61%

    Intervention : Structured Peer Observation and Coaching: Implement regular observation cycles with feedback; assign Mentor Teachers (MTs) in schools. School Leadership Mentorship: Train Principals and Head Teachers in mentorship; establish BRC-CRC mentoring teams for bi-monthly classroom observations. Technology-Enabled Mentorship: Utilize DIKSHA and NTP for digital mentor-mentee interactions and best practice sharing. Capacity Building: Promote NCERTs NISHTHA training for peer learning; conduct BRC or CRC-led workshops. Recognition and Incentives: Provide certifications and career benefits for active participation. Holistic Progress Card (HPC): Implement PARAKH NCERT framework to track mentoring engagement. Samagra Shiksha Abhiyan (SSA): Supports school-based mentoring programs. NISHTHA (NCERT): Focuses on peer learning and teacher training. DIKSHA Portal: Digital platform for mentorship and resource sharing. Rashtriya Madhyamik Shiksha Abhiyan (RMSA): Enhances teacher professional development. PM eVIDYA: Provides digital learning resources for teachers. National Initiative for School Heads and Teachers Holistic Advancement (NISHTHA 2): Strengthens pedagogical skills. National Professional Standards for Teachers (NPST): Encourages structured teacher mentoring. AICTE Training and Learning (ATAL) Program: Supports continuous teacher upskilling.Read More

  • Percentage of teachers do not participate in the ICT related training during the last 12 months54%

    Intervention : Mandatory ICT Training for All Teachers: Integrate digital literacy modules in NISHTHA and DIKSHA platforms. Organize annual ICT training under SCERTs and DIETs with a focus on AI, coding, and digital assessments. Strengthening ICT Infrastructure in Schools: Equip schools with smart classrooms, digital boards, and government-sponsored EdTech solutions (eg, PM eVidya). Provide access to free and open-source digital tools (GeoGebra, PHET simulations, etc.). Recognition and Incentives for Digital Learning Implementation: Establish “ICT Teacher of the Month” awards for innovative use of technology. Provide additional resources to schools with high teacher participation in ICT programs. DIKSHA platform offers digital training programs for teachers. PM eVidya supports digital infrastructure development in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school Principal/Heard Teacher undergo training on NEP2020/NCF-FS2023/NCF-SE2023/HPCN/A

    Intervention : Mandatory Training for School Leadership on Educational Reforms: Ensure all Principals and Head Teachers complete annual certification on NEP 2020 and NCF updates via DIKSHA. Conduct district-level workshops on implementing NCF and HPC strategies. Integration of Leadership Training in BRC and CRC Programs: Establish Principal Learning Circles (PLCs) for leadership development. Organize quarterly leadership reflection meetings on innovative pedagogy. Collaboration with National and State Training Institutions: Partner with NCERT, SCERTs, and NUEPA (National University of Educational Planning and Administration) for leadership training. Provide financial grants for Head Teachers to attend national and international leadership programs. NEP 2020 mandates leadership training for all Principals and Head Teachers. NUEPA offers specialized school leadership programs.Read More

  • Percentage of school Principal/Heard Teacher undergo any school leadership training programme organized by NIEPA or state governmentN/A

    Intervention : Mandatory Leadership Training Programs: Enforce compulsory training for school leaders under NCSL-NIEPA modules. Integrate state-specific leadership training workshops under Samagra Shiksha Abhiyan (SSA). Capacity-Building Initiatives: Conduct mentorship programs where experienced principals coach newly appointed heads. Establish a peer-learning network for school leaders to share best practices. Encouraging Participation in Online Courses: Promote DIKSHA, NISHTHA, and MOOCs (Massive Open Online Courses) for leadership training. Provide incentives (career progression, certificates, financial benefits) for participation. NEP 2020 emphasizes leadership training for school heads to ensure quality education. NIEPAs NCSL offers structured leadership programs for Principals and Head Teachers.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session/workshop on Stress ManagementN/A

    Intervention : Integrating Stress Management into Teacher Development Plans: Conduct quarterly stress management workshops in collaboration with mental health professionals. Implement mindfulness and yoga sessions under Fit India Movement. Providing Counselling and Peer Support: Establish teacher support groups for discussing stress and workload issues. Offer free access to counseling services through tie-ups with NGOs and mental health organizations. Workload Reduction Strategies: Implement smart lesson planning and workload-sharing techniques. Promote flexible work hours and time-off policies for teachers under stress. NCERT promotes Yoga and stress reduction techniques in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session/workshop on Managing emotions/Emotional IntelligenceN/A

    Intervention : Mandatory Emotional Intelligence (EI) Training for Teachers: Conduct workshops on self-awareness, self-regulation, empathy, and social skills. Provide EI assessment tools for teachers to track their emotional growth. Integration of SEL (Social-Emotional Learning) in Teacher Training: Train teachers in identifying and managing student emotions in classrooms. Develop classroom activities focused on mindfulness and emotional expression. Leadership in Emotional Intelligence: Encourage Principals to undergo EI training to create a positive school culture. Integrate EI strategies in student discipline and conflict resolution. PARAKH NCERT emphasize emotional intelligence in teacher training modules. NISHTHA training includes SEL components for teachers.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session/workshop on Mental Health awarenessN/A

    Intervention : Implement Mental Health Training Programs in Schools: Train teachers to identify early signs of student mental health issues. Collaborate with psychologists and counselors for periodic training. Establish School-Based Mental Health Support Systems: Introduce student mental health support groups led by trained teachers. Promote helpline numbers (eg, Snehi, Vandrevala Foundation) for student counseling. Policy Integration and Awareness Drives: Conduct annual mental health awareness campaigns. Integrate mental well-being discussions in morning assemblies. NCERT issued guidelines for mental health promotion in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session/workshop on Behavioural Management in a classroomN/A

    Intervention : Workshops and Training Sessions: Conduct professional development programs on classroom discipline without corporal punishment. Positive Reinforcement Techniques: Promote reward-based approaches for behavior correction. Structured Behavior Management Framework: Develop clear guidelines for handling disruptive behavior, aligned with NCERTs Guidelines on School Discipline. Restorative Justice Practices: Train teachers in conflict resolution through dialogue and mediation. Peer Observation and Feedback System: Facilitate structured classroom observations for teachers to learn from one another. Digital Training Resources: Use platforms like DIKSHA for online behavioral management modules. Holistic Progress Card (HPC): Integrate PARAKH NCERTs framework to assess teachers effectiveness in classroom behavior management. Right to Education (RTE) Act: Bans corporal punishment and promotes positive discipline. National Initiative for School Heads and Teachers Holistic Advancement (NISHTHA): Offers structured training on behavioral management. PM eVIDYA: Provides online modules on effective classroom management strategies. Integrated Teacher Education Programme (ITEP): Focuses on pre-service teacher training, including classroom behavior management. Adolescence Education Programme (AEP): Addresses behavioral challenges and positive discipline in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session/workshop on Managing and understanding Adolescent behaviourN/A

    Intervention : Workshops on Adolescent Psychology and Challenges: Train teachers in understanding hormonal, emotional, and cognitive changes in adolescents. Educate teachers on cyber safety, peer pressure, and substance abuse risks. Peer Counseling Programs: Appoint trained student peer counselors to support adolescent students. Organize interactive sessions with psychologists and social workers. Parental Awareness Sessions: Conduct joint teacher-parent workshops on adolescent behavior. Provide resource materials on adolescent development and parenting strategies. Adolescence Education Program (AEP) by NCERT promotes adolescent awareness in schools.Read More

  • Percentage of school organized any Teacher training session or workshop for parents around understanding their children better or managing their behaviourN/A

    Intervention : Mandatory Parental Awareness Workshops: Conduct quarterly parenting sessions in collaboration with mental health experts. Provide behavioral guidance through digital resources and parenting handbooks. Building Strong School-Parent Partnerships: Introduce regular parent-teacher meetings to discuss child behavior and well-being. Create WhatsApp groups or digital forums for parents to share experiences and solutions. Counseling Support for Parents: Establish parent counseling helplines for behavioral concerns. Offer one-on-one sessions for parents struggling with behavioral management. NEP 2020 stresses the role of parents in holistic child development.Read More

  • Percentage of school does not offer any regular Professional Development sessions for teaching staffN/A

    Intervention : Structured CPD Framework: Implement annual Continuing Professional Development (CPD) sessions, ensuring teachers complete 50 hours as mandated by NEP 2020. Digital Learning Platforms: Promote DIKSHA, SWAYAM, NISHTHA, and PM eVIDYA for continuous, certification-based upskilling. Blended Learning Approach: Combine online and offline professional development programs, including workshops and interactive training. Reflective Practice and Peer Learning: Establish teacher learning circles, conduct peer observations, and introduce mentoring programs for knowledge sharing. Subject-Specific Training: Align CPD sessions with NCF 2023, focusing on competency-based teaching, assessment strategies, and student engagement. Expert-Led Workshops: Collaborate with NCERT, SCERTs, CBSE, and state education bodies to conduct regular training with education experts. Integration with Holistic Progress Card (HPC): Use PARAKH NCERTs professional development assessment tools to track teacher progress. NISHTHA (National Initiative for School Heads and Teachers Holistic Advancement): Large-scale teacher training aligned with NEP 2020. DIKSHA (Digital Infrastructure for Knowledge Sharing): Provides free teacher training modules. SWAYAM (Study Webs of Active-Learning for Young Aspiring Minds): Online CPD courses with certification. PM eVIDYA: Digital learning initiative including teacher training. National Professional Standards for Teachers (NPST): Establishes quality benchmarks for teacher development. NCERT CPD Modules: Online and offline training resources for subject-specific pedagogy. Rashtriya Madhyamik Shiksha Abhiyan (RMSA): Funds teacher training programs at the secondary level.Read More
